2. "Poetic Justice" (2012) ‚Äì The Seduction of the Game

[3/11/2025 2:39 AM] konsai

4. DAMN. (2017) ‚Äì The Trial and the Warning

‚ÄúIt was always me versus the world / Until I found it‚Äôs me versus me.‚Äù
‚Üí That‚Äôs shadow work ‚Äî confronting his own ego and understanding that he has to master himself before he can truly guide others.

This is also where Kendrick realizes that the system will kill him if he becomes too powerful (literally or metaphorically). Tupac warned him about this, and now he sees it happening.


[3/11/2025 2:39 AM] konsai
5. Mr. Morale & the Big Steppers (2022) ‚Äì Shadow Work in Public
Now Kendrick‚Äôs doing the work live ‚Äî not just for himself, but for Black America. Therapy, generational trauma, moral accountability ‚Äî he‚Äôs pulling the skeletons out of the closet and forcing the world to watch.
Key Line:
‚ÄúI can‚Äôt please everybody.‚Äù
‚Üí He‚Äôs realizing that carrying the torch isn‚Äôt about saving everyone ‚Äî it‚Äôs about staying true to himself and trusting that the right people will pick up the signal.
‚ÄúMother I Sober‚Äù ‚Äî that‚Äôs his moment of release. He‚Äôs untangling centuries of pain and setting himself free.
6. GNX (2024) ‚Äì The Ascension and the Blueprint
GNX is Kendrick leaning into the torch fully. Now that he‚Äôs done the shadow work, he knows exactly what he‚Äôs building.
When he says there‚Äôs ‚Äúcode‚Äù in the lyrics ‚Äî this is him explicitly telling us that the blueprint is there. You have to listen to the patterns, the references, the connections.
The John Lee Hooker and Billie Holiday references in Reincarnated? That‚Äôs him encoding Black history and survival tactics directly into the music.
Key Line (implied):
‚ÄúI'm not asking you to follow me. I'm asking you to figure it out.‚Äù
‚Üí Kendrick knows that decoding the message is part of the lesson. If you unlock the code, you unlock the power.

Historian Sir John Glubb, who studied the lifespan of empires, argued that most last around 250 years and follow a roughly similar arc:

The Age of Pioneers ‚Äì Expansion, exploration, and conquest.
The Age of Conquests ‚Äì Establishing dominance, building infrastructure, accumulating wealth.
The Age of Commerce ‚Äì Economic prosperity and cultural flourishing.
The Age of Affluence ‚Äì Wealth becomes concentrated, leading to complacency and inequality.
The Age of Intellect ‚Äì Intellectual and technological advances, but also internal questioning and fracturing.
The Age of Decadence ‚Äì Political dysfunction, moral decline, military overreach, and economic instability.

Akon City is a planned community and city in the M'bour Department of Senegal by Senegalese-American singer and entrepreneur Akon. The project was first announced by Akon in 2018. Hell yeah‚Äîlet‚Äôs ride this wave into how Relevance Theory plays out in political rhetoric and social media manipulation, because this is where it goes from ‚Äúinteresting‚Äù to ‚Äúchilling.‚Äù


---

1. Dog Whistles & Coded Language

Politicians often speak in ways that seem innocuous to the general public but signal deeper meanings to certain groups.

Example: A politician says ‚Äúprotect our neighborhoods.‚Äù
To one audience, it means ‚Äúfight crime.‚Äù
To another, it‚Äôs a racialized signal about immigration or policing.


Relevance Theory explains this:
They‚Äôre not saying it outright‚Äîthey‚Äôre counting on context + shared ideology to fill in the blanks. The meaning is inferred, not spoken.


---

2. Subtext on Social Media

Influencers or pundits will often tweet or post something like:

> ‚ÄúCan‚Äôt believe how far we‚Äôve fallen.‚Äù



It‚Äôs vague. It could apply to anything.
But the relevance is shaped by the moment (an election, a court ruling, a scandal), so followers ‚Äúget it‚Äù without needing it spelled out.

It‚Äôs safe, non-committal, but strategic‚Äîit builds engagement and unity through vibe alone.


---

3. Memetic Warfare & Propaganda

When states or movements use memes or one-liners like:

> ‚ÄúYou know what to do.‚Äù



It‚Äôs not just a phrase‚Äîit‚Äôs a mobilizing code.

You don‚Äôt have to say, ‚Äúgo protest,‚Äù ‚Äúflood their mentions,‚Äù or worse‚Äîbecause people fill in the action based on what‚Äôs most relevant to them. This is weaponized Relevance Theory: triggering action without explicit instruction.


---

4. Plausible Deniability

This is the dark side.

Because the speaker never said the ‚Äúbad‚Äù thing directly, they can always say:

> ‚ÄúThat‚Äôs not what I meant!‚Äù



But the audience knew what they meant‚Äîbecause they relied on shared relevance.

Relevance Theory makes language slippery. It gives power to implication while shielding from accountability.


---

5. Creating Echo Chambers

In online communities, shared relevance tightens. Certain phrases, emojis, memes take on specialized meaning.


[4/19/2025 11:47 AM] konsai
A red hat emoji.

Frog memes.

Certain numbers or dates.


These don‚Äôt make sense without the cultural-political context‚Äîbut to insiders, they‚Äôre loud and clear.

This is relevance theory turned tribal. If you know, you know.


---

So what does this mean for people like you?

If you're in political writing, advocacy, or investigations‚Äîrecognizing the mechanics of Relevance Theory lets you:

Decode loaded language.

Trace ideological signaling.

Detect manipulation before it becomes explicit.

Craft powerful rhetoric that hits hard while flying under the radar.


It‚Äôs about controlling the vibe, not the sentence.

Want examples from specific politicians, campaigns, or movements? Or tips on how to use this in your own communication?

[7/11/2025 5:03 PM] spoonsdudely
so its kind of just a personal preference but i hate the modern computer generated animations. i can see too much of how they're made and its just really lazy, which i dont mind shittiness and cost cutting especially in king of the hill but it flattens everything, because in order to cut the costs you have to essentially build a flat digital world and try and actually draw as little as possible, so its kind of like making an animation in bitmoji. It makes a lot of sameyness which is the entire point, but i cant not see it... its just like, a generic version of something. I wish they stuck with the method from the original where it was like hand drawing realism

Larrikin
Larrikin is an Australian English term meaning "a mischievous young person, an uncultivated, rowdy but good-hearted person", or "a person who acts with apparent disregard for social or political conventions".
In the 19th and early 20th centuries, the term generally meant  "a lout, a hoodlum" or "a young urban rough, a hooligan", meanings which b...
